<span class="italic"><a title="Link to journal home page" href="https://doi.org/10.1039/1463-9270/1999">Green Chem.</a></span>, 2023, <strong>25</strong>, 8286-8294</div><h1 id="sect181"><span class="title_heading">Carbon-coated ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> hierarchical nanospheres to inhibit polysulfide dissolution in ether-based electrolytes for high-performance Na-ion batteries<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span></h1><p class="header_text">
      <span class="bold">
        
          
            Jun 
            Xu
          
        
      </span><span class="orcid"><a target="_blank" title="Select to open ORCID record for Jun&nbsp;Xu (orcid.org/0000-0001-9829-4382) in a new window" id="connect-orcid-link" href="http://orcid.org/0000-0001-9829-4382"><img id="orcid-id-logo" src="/content/NewImages/orcid_16x16.png" alt="ORCID logo"></a></span>*,

      <br><span class="italic">School of Microelectronics and Instrumental Analysis Center, Hefei University of Technology, Hefei 230009, P. R. China. E-mail: <a href="mailto:apjunxu@hfut.edu.cn">apjunxu@hfut.edu.cn</a>; <a href="mailto:zhangyan@hfut.edu.cn">zhangyan@hfut.edu.cn</a>; <a href="mailto:k.xing@hfut.edu.cn">k.xing@hfut.edu.cn</a></span>
    </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      10th July 2023
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 12th September 2023</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 13th September 2023</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>In this work, we report a simple hydrothermal route coupled with post-carbonization treatment to synthesize novel ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C hierarchical nanospheres as an advanced sodium storage anode in ether-based electrolytes (EBEs). In the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C architectures, few-layered ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanosheets with an expanded interlayer spacing of 0.67 nm are self-assembled to form hierarchical nanospheres, providing a robust structure and a large surface area that facilitate electrolyte contact in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). The amorphous carbon coating plays key roles in not only improving the electronic conductivity but also inhibiting the shuttle effect of polysulfides in EBEs, which results in superior high-rate capability and excellent cyclability. Consequently, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode yields a high specific capacity of 185 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at an ultra-high current density of 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and maintains a specific capacity of 209 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after undergoing 3000 cycles at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> as the highest current density for long-term cycling to date. Compared with carbonate-based electrolytes (CBEs), the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode containing EBEs shows a significantly prolonged cycling lifespan and improved high-rate capability. Moreover, the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell is demonstrated for the first time and delivers decent cycling performance of 300 cycles at 1C with a capacity retention of 95.9%. Our work provides new insight into enhancing the sodium storage performance of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes by nanoscale engineering and electrolyte modulation.</p></div><hr>
    
      <h2 id="sect260"><span class="a_heading">Introduction</span></h2>
      <span>Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely employed in various applications including portable electronic devices, electric vehicles (EVs) and other renewable energy storage systems over the past decades. However, the rapidly increasing demands for low-cost energy storage are seriously restricted by the scarcity and high cost of lithium resources.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15</span></sup></a> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are currently regarded as one of the most promising alternatives to LIBs in the next generation owing to the abundance and low price of sodium resources and their similar electrochemical mechanisms to LIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit6"><sup><span class="sup_ref">68</span></sup></a> However, serious problems such as large volume expansions and slow kinetics generally occur in SIBs due to the larger ionic radius and heavier mass of Na-ions. Poor electrochemical performance, especially in the aspects of high-rate capability and cycling stability, is suffered by SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit9"><sup><span class="sup_ref">9,10</span></sup></a> Therefore, it is urgent but full of challenges to improve the electrochemical performance of SIBs <span class="italic">via</span> combinational strategies, such as exploration of advanced electrode materials, utilization of appropriate electrolytes, <span class="italic">etc</span>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit11"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1115</span></sup></a></span>
      <p class="otherpara">As an emerging representative material of layered transition metal dichalcogenides (LTMDs), rhenium disulfide (ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>) has recently attracted increasing attention in various application fields such as electrocatalysis, electrochemical energy storage, optoelectronics, <span class="italic">etc</span>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit16"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1619</span></sup></a> The layered structure with a large interlayer spacing of 0.61 nm and extremely weak interlayer van der Waals (vdWs) interactions (18 meV for ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small><span class="italic">vs.</span> 460 meV for MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>) makes it highly suitable for alkali-ion batteries, especially for storage of Na-ions that have large ion sizes.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit20"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2023</span></sup></a> ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> has a theoretical specific capacity of 428 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> for sodium storage with intercalation coupled with a conversion mechanism. Similar to other LTMDs, however, the poor electronic conductivity and structural aggregation in the conversion reaction inevitably restrict the electrochemical performance and hinder the practical application of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> in SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit24"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2426</span></sup></a> To address these issues, much effort has been devoted to constructing ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> composites that integrate high electrical conductivity and structural stability simultaneously. For example, Zhao and co-workers reported the synthesis of 1T-ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanosheets confined to a reduced graphene oxide interlayer and N-doped carbon coating (rGO@ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>@NC) for outstanding sodium storage performance in NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small>/ethylene carbonate (EC) and diethyl carbonate (DEC), exhibiting high-rate performance of 231 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and excellent cycling stability at 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> for 4000 cycles.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27</span></sup></a> Liu <span class="italic">et al.</span> prepared MXene@ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>@C composite anodes possessing improved electrochemical performances (202 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 200 cycles) using the NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> in EC/DEC electrolyte.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28</span></sup></a> Despite the progress achieved, the sodium storage performances of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes in carbonate-based electrolytes (CBEs) were unsatisfactory, especially at high current densities. The cycling performance at a current density over 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> has been scarcely investigated. On the other hand, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are attracting increasing attention for SIBs, as they have numerous advantages including high ion transport, a stable solvation structure of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>, high lowest unoccupied molecular orbital (LUMO) levels of solvated Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> to form a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer, and highly reversible solvent co-intercalation reactions.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit29"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2935</span></sup></a> Therefore, utilization of EBEs is expected to be an effective strategy to improve the sodium storage performance of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. Nevertheless, it was pointed out that the shuttling effect of polysulfides is encountered in EBEs for metal sulfide anodes during the discharge/charge processes, giving rise to the under-voltage failure phenomenon.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> To date, the sodiation/desodiation mechanism of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes in EBEs has been rarely investigated.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">In this work, carbon-coated ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C) hierarchical nanospheres are designed as an advanced anode for high-performance SIBs containing EBEs. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres are synthesized by a facile hydrothermal route followed by glucose carbonization. Few-layered 1T-ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanosheets with expanded interlayer spacing are self-assembled ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres with diameters of 3050 nm. When being evaluated as an anode material in SIBs, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres deliver significantly improved electrochemical performance in EBEs than in CBEs, including superior high-rate capability (186 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and excellent cycling stability (3000 cycles) at a high current density of 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The effect of diverse electrolytes on the performance of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes is investigated. It is found that the voltage failure phenomenon is attributed to the shuttling effect of polysulfides and side reactions of sulfides with copper current collectors and can be greatly retarded by an amorphous carbon coating on ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres, thereby resulting in improved capacity and cyclability. Furthermore, the electrochemical performance of Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cells containing EBEs is investigated, revealing great potential for practical applications in SIBs.</p>
    
    
      <h2 id="sect320"><span class="a_heading">Results and discussion</span></h2>
      <span>The synthesis procedure of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres is illustrated in <a title="Select to navigate to scheme" href="#imgsch1">Scheme 1</a>. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> hierarchical nanospheres self-assembled from few-layered nanosheets were hydrothermally synthesized at 180 C for 24 h using ammonium perrhenate and thioacetamide as the starting materials. The as-prepared ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres were then evenly mixed with glucose and underwent thermal annealing at 600 C. As a result, carbonization of glucose to form an amorphous carbon coating and recrystallization of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> are achieved. The resulting ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C with an amorphous carbon coating is expected to play key roles in two aspects. On the one hand, the carbon coating could increase the electronic conductivity favourable for high-rate performance; on the other hand, the carbon coating could anchor soluble polysulfide species and suppress their shuttling and side reactions, contributing to stable cycling performance.</span>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgsch1"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-s1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-s1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-s1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Scheme 1 </b> <span id="sch1"><span class="graphic_title">Schematic illustration describing the synthesis of amorphous carbon coated ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> hierarchical nanospheres for SIBs.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The morphological features of the as-prepared ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C samples were examined by scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) observations. For the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> sample, it is clear that ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanosheets were self-assembled to nanospheres with a typical size of 3050 nm (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a and b</a>). The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanosheets have a layered structure and the interlayer spacing is estimated to be 0.67 nm as shown in the high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) image (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c</a>). The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C sample obtained after 600 C carbonization can well reserve the hierarchical spherical morphology (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1d and e</a>), indicating its excellent thermal stability. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres encapsulated by a carbon coating are connected very tightly. The HRTEM image of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1f</a>, indicating that the interlayer spacing of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> is also 0.67 nm, which is much larger than the normal value (0.61 nm). The interlayer expansion is probably attributed to lattice distortion coupled with the extremely weak interlayer coupling.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit19"><sup><span class="sup_ref">19,22</span></sup></a> The enlarged interlayer spacing could reduce the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> diffusion barrier and promote fast Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> insertion/extraction, thus contributing to the acceleration of the electrochemical reaction kinetics of SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit5"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5,37</span></sup></a><a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1g</a> shows a TEM image of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres and the corresponding energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) elemental mappings of Re, S and C. The homogeneous distribution of the C element verifies the formation of a uniform conductive network throughout the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres. The atomic ratio of Re<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">:<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">S is about 1<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">:<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">1.88 (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1h</a>), indicating the existence of some sulfur vacancies in ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C. Thermogravimetry (TG) fails to evaluate the carbon content of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C (Fig. S1<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), which is attributed to the low boiling point of the resulting Re<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> converted from ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. The carbon content of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C was found to be approximately 12.6 wt% using an elemental analyzer. Nitrogen adsorptiondesorption measurements were performed to quantitatively investigate the surface area (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1i</a>). A typical IV isotherm with a hysteresis loop at a high relative pressure is observed for ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C, offering a large BrunauerEmmettTeller (BET) surface area of 103.2 m<small><sup>2</sup></small> g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The high BET surface area is attributed to the few-layered thickness and the hierarchical structure and is beneficial for providing good interfacial contact with the electrolyte in discharge/charge processes. In addition, the electronic conductivities of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres before and after carbon coating were measured by using a four-probe tester. ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C exhibits a dramatically enhanced conductivity with a value of about 3.8  10<small><sup>2</sup></small> S cm<small><sup>1</sup></small>, which is much higher than that of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (3.4  10<small><sup>4</sup></small> S cm<small><sup>1</sup></small>). Therefore, the carbon coating layer over the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres builds a highly conductive 3D network and provides sufficient channels for fast electron transport. Therefore, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres featuring a hierarchical structure, few-layered thickness, expanded interlayer spacing, a large surface area, and high conductivity are promising as robust anodes for sodium storage.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">(ac) SEM, TEM and HRTEM images of the pristine ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres. (df) SEM, TEM and HRTEM images of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres, (g) TEM image and the corresponding EDS elemental mappings of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres. (h) EDS spectrum of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres. (i) Nitrogen adsorptiondesorption isotherms of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a>. For both samples, the characteristic peaks from ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> at 13.7, 32.6, 43.6 and 57.2 are clearly distinguishable, corresponding to the (001), (2<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_0032_0304.gif" alt="[2 with combining macron]">0), (003), and (22<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_0031_0304.gif" alt="[1 with combining macron]">) diffraction of 1T-ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (JCPDF No. 52-0818). Obviously, the (001) peak is slightly shifted to a lower 2<span class="italic"></span> degree, indicating expanded interlayer spacing, which is in agreement with the HRTEM observations. The Raman spectra of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b</a>. In both cases, there are two peaks located at 150 and 211 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small>, corresponding respectively to the E<small><sub>g</sub></small> mode from the in-plane vibration and the A<small><sub>g</sub></small> mode from the out-of-plane vibration of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit23"><sup><span class="sup_ref">23,38</span></sup></a> Moreover, some additional weak peaks in the range of 100400 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> are also observed, which are derived from the distorted 1T structure of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> with asymmetry.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit39"><sup><span class="sup_ref">39</span></sup></a> Notably, two obvious broad bands at 1340 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> (disorder-induced D-band) and 1580 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> (graphitic G-band) are detected for ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C, confirming the formation of an amorphous carbon layer by glucose carbonization.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit40"><sup><span class="sup_ref">40,41</span></sup></a> X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was conducted to further investigate the chemical states and bonding configurations in ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. The survey spectra in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2c</a> show obvious signals of Re, S, C, and O elements in ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C, supporting the formation of an amorphous carbon layer with functional oxygen-containing groups on the surfaces of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres. The high-resolution Re 4f spectra exhibit two characteristic peaks of Re 4f<small><sub>5/2</sub></small> and Re 4f<small><sub>7/2</sub></small> at 44.6 and 42.2 eV (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2d</a>), confirming the existence of Re<small><sup>4+</sup></small> in both ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2e</a> presents the high-resolution S 2p spectra of two samples. The profiles could be split into two peaks located at 162.7 eV (S 2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small>) and 163.9 eV (S 2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small>), indicating the existence of sulfides (S<small><sup>2</sup></small>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42</span></sup></a> Moreover, the high-resolution C 1s spectrum of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2f</a> can be deconvoluted into two peaks of CC (284.7 eV) and CO (285.9 eV), respectively.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">(a) XRD patterns of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. (b) Raman spectra of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. (cf) XPS spectra of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">To evaluate the sodium storage performance of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C, CR2032 type coin-cells containing the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small>/DEGDME electrolyte were assembled. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a> shows the comparative rate capacities of the two anodes ranging from 0.2 to 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode presents higher average reversible capacities of 426, 406, 386, 332, 281, 241 and 185 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10 and 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. However, the corresponding specific capacities of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode are relatively lower and reach 403, 363, 322, 292, 240, 178 and 115 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. The pristine C anode obtained by annealing glucose at 600 C exhibits even lower specific capacities (below 100 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). When the current density returns to 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode recovers to a high reversible capacity of 439 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, while the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode regains a decreased discharge capacity of only 342 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. This observation reflects the enhanced reversibility of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C. More importantly, such excellent capacities of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C at various current densities are much higher than those of the previously reported ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes in CBEs, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3b</a>. The high-rate performances in these reports are mainly evaluated below 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, except Qiao <span class="italic">et al.</span> reported that the rGO@ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>@NC electrode had a reversible capacity of 231 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27</span></sup></a> Notably, the specific capacity of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C in our case can reach as high as 241 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Remarkably, excellent high-rate performance at an ultra-high current density of 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> is achieved for the first time, yielding a high capacity of 186 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Therefore, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode exhibits higher capacities than those of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes at all current densities (Table S1<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>).</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">Electrochemical performances of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C, ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, and C anodes in the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small>/DEGDME electrolyte. (a) Rate capability of three anodes at various current densities from 0.2 to 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (b) comparison of the rate capability of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes for SIBs; (c) GITT curves; (d) the <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> values in different discharge/charge states of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes; (e) Nyquist plots of two anodes before cycling; (f) cycling performance and the corresponding coulombic efficiencies of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes at 1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (g) cycling performance and the corresponding coulombic efficiencies of the three anodes at 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was used to evaluate the diffusion coefficient of Na ions (<span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small>) in the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes, and the corresponding curves are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3c</a>. The <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> value can be calculated from the equation expressed as <a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-t1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-t1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-t1.gif"></a>, where <span class="italic">L</span> is the Na-ion diffusion length that can be equal to the thickness of the dense electrode, <span class="italic"></span> is the constant current pulse time, <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> is the potential difference in the steady state voltage of the step at the plateau, and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub><span class="italic"></span></sub></small> is the potential change during a constant current pulse time excluding the <span class="italic">iR</span> drop.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42,43</span></sup></a> Based on the GITT results, the calculated <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> values of the two anodes from each pulse are displayed in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3d</a>. They have the same <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> variation trends during the discharge and charge processes. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode exhibits <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> values in the range of 10<small><sup>9</sup></small>10<small><sup>11</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, which are higher than those of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode in both sodiation and desodiation states. This indicates that the carbon coating encapsulating the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres could facilitate the fast diffusion of Na ions and increase the reaction kinetics. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3e</a> depicts the Nyquist plots of two anodes before cycling and the corresponding equivalent circuit model is shown in the inset, where <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> and <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> represent the series resistance and the charge transfer resistance at the collector/electrolyte interface, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44,45</span></sup></a> Both curves show similar profiles possessing a semicircle in the high-frequency range and an oblique line in the low-frequency range. It is obvious that the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode delivers a lower <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value (173 ) than that of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode (245 ), which further proves improved charge transfer in the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The cycling performances of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes at 1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3f</a>. A high reversible capacity of 328 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> is maintained after 1000 cycles with a capacity retention of 83.5% for the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode, whereas the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode keeps a capacity of 222 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 400 cycles with a low capacity retention of only 63.4%. Remarkably, when galvanically cycled at 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode can present an impressive cyclability of 2500 cycles with a maintained capacity of 198 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, thus yielding a capacity retention of 70.2% (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3g</a>). Significantly increased capacities and improved cycling lifespans are achieved by ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C relative to ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>. The pristine C anode has rather low specific capacities, but shows excellent cycling stability and a long cycle lifespan. There is an abnormal under-voltage failure observed for the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36,46</span></sup></a> Fig. S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> displays the last three discharge/charge curves of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode after cycling at 1 and 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. The abnormal cycle failures generally occur as the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> cells fail to reach a given cut-off voltage while being charged.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">More surprisingly, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode can even be cycled at a current density as high as 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4a</a>). It exhibits a high specific capacity of 209 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 3000 cycles and presents an extremely low attenuation rate of 0.0031% per cycle, further verifying its excellent long-term cycling stability in EBEs. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode exhibiting such remarkable high-rate cyclability surpasses the previously reported ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4b</a> and Table S1<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The SEM image of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode after cycling is presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4c</a>. It clearly reveals that the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres can well retain their original interconnected spherical morphology after cycling, which is responsible for their outstanding cycling performance. On the other hand, the pristine ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode can also operate over 2400 cycles at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and maintain a reversible capacity of 136 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Unfortunately, the under-voltage failure is also observed for ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> when the cycle number extends to 2453 at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4d</a>). Abnormal cycle failure leads to infinite charging below the cutoff voltage. This phenomenon is believed to be caused by the dissolution and escape of polysulfide intermediates in the EBEs, leading to the occurrence of the shuttle effect.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36,47</span></sup></a> The dissolved polysulfides could further react with the copper current collector, thus leading to current collector corrosion and the formation of possible impurities of copper sulfides. In order to verify this speculation, the cells with ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes after cycling were dismantled to observe the color change of the separators and the current collectors, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4e</a>. Compared with the original white separator (i), there is an obvious yellow intermediate substance stuck to the spent glass fiber separator from the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> cell (iii), while the separator from the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C cell (ii) has negligible colour change. This observation supports the fact that the shuttling effect of polysulfides diffused through the separator could be inhibited by the carbon coating. On the other hand, the copper current collectors from the two cells after cycling were also investigated after removing the electrode materials by an ultrasonication treatment. It is observed that the copper foil from the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode was seriously corroded and became black more obviously relative to the one from ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C. The Raman spectra of the two copper current collectors were obtained in the black regions (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4f</a>). Two peaks located at 268 and 473 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> can be attributed to the vibrational stretching mode from the CuS bond and the vibrational stretching mode from the covalent SS bond of S<small><sup>2</sup></small> ions, respectively, thus indicating the formation of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S on the surfaces.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> A side reaction might take place in the charge process as 2Cu + S<small><sup>2</sup></small>  Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S + 2e<small><sup></sup></small>. By contrast, the less black color on the copper foil and the lower Raman signals of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S imply that the side reaction to form Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>S is significantly suppressed in the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode owing to the enhanced strong anchoring of sulfide species by the amorphous carbon coating.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Cycling performances and the corresponding coulombic efficiencies of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anodes in the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small>/DEGDME electrolyte at a high current density of 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (b) cycling performance comparison of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-based anodes for SIBs; (c) the SEM image of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode after 3000 cycles at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (d) the last three discharge/charge curves of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> anode at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (e) the original separator and current collector (i), and those from the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C (ii) and ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (iii) cells after cycling at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> for 600 cycles; (f) Raman spectra of the two current collectors in the black regions after cycling in panel (e).</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">In order to uncover the influences of electrolytes on Na-ion storage behaviours, the electrochemical performances of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes in diverse electrolytes such as NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME, NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in EC/PC, and NaClO<small><sub>6</sub></small> in EC/PC were investigated. The rate performances of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes with different electrolytes were compared at current densities ranging from 0.1 to 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5a</a>. Apparently, the specific capacities of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode in DEGDME are overall higher than those in EC/PC. Interestingly, NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> and NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in the EC/PC system show almost the same rate performance. The initial coulombic efficiencies (ICEs) of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode with NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> in EC/PC, NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in EC/PC and NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolytes are 78%, 86% and 88%, respectively. This observation is consistent with the previous reports on high ICEs and reversible capacities in EBEs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit23"><sup><span class="sup_ref">23,49</span></sup></a><a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5b</a> reveals that the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C cell with the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte has a significantly decreased <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> (173 ), which is much smaller than those of the cells containing the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in EC/PC electrolyte (870 ) and the NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> in EC/PC electrolyte (1005 ). <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5c</a> shows the cycling performances of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes at 1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> in various electrolytes. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode maintains a stable reversible capacity of 328 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 1000 cycles in the NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte, delivering a capacity retention of 83.5%. However, the two cells containing EC/PC show deteriorated cyclability. The capacity of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode decays rapidly to 134 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> within 400 cycles in the NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> in EC/PC electrolyte. Compared with the NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> electrolyte, the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> electrolytes exhibit more stable cycling performance, which is probably attributed to the decent solubility and dissociation degree of PF<small><sub>6</sub></small><small><sup></sup></small> to form stable SEI layers.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35,50</span></sup></a> Therefore, it is demonstrated that the NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte is beneficial for high ICEs, stable cycling performance, and high-rate capability for ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C electrodes.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Rate performance of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes in different electrolytes; (b) Nyquist plots of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes in different electrolytes; (c) cycling performance of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anodes in different electrolytes at 1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>; (d) the galvanostatic cycling curves of the NaNa cells containing different electrolytes at 0.1 mA cm<small><sup>2</sup></small>, (e) the enlarged view of the voltage curves in the duration of 5055 h; (f) Nyquist plots of the NaNa symmetrical cells containing different electrolytes; (g) Nyquist plots of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/CReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C symmetrical cells containing different electrolytes.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The discharge/charge behaviours of NaNa symmetric cells containing different electrolytes were investigated at a constant current of 0.1 mA cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> for 250 h (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5d</a>). The cell containing the NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte provides a more stable and much smaller polarization voltage for continuous cycles, indicating its outstanding cycling stability in the EBE.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51,52</span></sup></a><a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5e</a> highlights the five-hour curves of the NaNa cells containing CBEs and EBEs after cycling for 50 h. The overpotential of the cell in the NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte is stabilized at a low value of only 3.4 mV. The polarization voltage of each cycle in the EBE is stable, forming an output with a quasi-rectangular shape. However, the two types of EC/PC electrolytes have larger overpotentials (3070 mV) and apparent potential fluctuations, giving a trapezoid or U-shape. The dramatic variation in potential is associated with the continuous decomposition of the electrolyte during the discharge/charge processes and thus leads to negative effects on cycling performance.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51,52</span></sup></a> The Nyquist plots of the NaNa symmetrical cells containing various electrolytes are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5f</a>. The <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> in DEGDME is only 4 , which is approximately two orders of magnitude smaller than those in the EC/PC systems. This suggests the formation of a thin and stable ether-based SEI layer in the DEGDME system, enabling a faster Na-ion transport rate across the SEI film.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit52"><sup><span class="sup_ref">52</span></sup></a> A similar phenomenon was observed in the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/CReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C symmetrical cells containing the different electrolytes (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5g</a>). The <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value is smallest for the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte (14 ), it increases to 22  for the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in EC/PC electrolyte, and further increases to 26  for the NaClO<small><sub>4</sub></small> in EC/PC electrolyte. All these results reveal that the NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte is more favorable for the high-rate sodium storage capability of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C electrode.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Therefore, it is found that the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode in the EBE exhibits significantly enhanced sodium storage performance, which could be due to the synergetic effects of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres encapsulated within the carbon coating layer and the EBE system. Firstly, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres having good structural stability are capable of mitigating the volume changes of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres during repeated cycles owing to the hierarchical architectures and the carbon coating. Secondly, the amorphous carbon coating on the surfaces of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres provides efficient conductive channels for the rapid transport of electrons. Thirdly, the surface carbon coating can effectively inhibit the dissolution and escape of polysulfide species in the EBE, thus inhibiting the occurrence of the shuttle effect and the under-voltage failure phenomenon.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> Finally, DEGDME as an EBE can provide high ionic conductivity, a stable solvation structure, thin and stable SEI layers, and fast charge transfer, which favours the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode to achieve enhanced electrochemical performance of SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit53"><sup><span class="sup_ref">53</span></sup></a></p>
      <p class="otherpara">Full cells of Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C containing the NaFP<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte were further fabricated by using the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode and the commercial Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> cathode. Pre-sodiation of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C anode was performed for the full cell fabrication. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6a</a> plots the discharge/charge curves of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C half cell, the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> half cell and the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell. The Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> cathode with a stable discharge plateau at 3.35 V (<span class="italic">vs.</span> Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/Na) has a reversible discharge capacity of 100 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.5C (1C = 117 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). The discharge/charge behaviour of the full cell was investigated in a voltage window of 3.81.0 V. The full cell delivers reversible discharge/charge capacities of 105/106 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.5C. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6b</a> presents the rate capability of the full cell, which yields an average discharge capacity of 106, 105, 103, 101, 89 and 54 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5 and 10C, respectively. Remarkably, the capacity can be restored to 105 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> as the rate returns to 0.2C. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6c</a> displays the cycling performance of the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell at 1C for 300 cycles. A capacity of 68 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> can be maintained after 300 cycles with an average attenuation rate of 0.097% per cycle, indicating outstanding cycling stability. Significantly, the application of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> in full cells with superior sodium storage performance is demonstrated for the first time in our work, indicating its great potential in practical applications.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3gc02488a-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2023/GC/d3gc02488a/d3gc02488a-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">Electrochemical performance of the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell containing the 1.0 mol L<small><sup>1</sup></small> NaPF<small><sub>6</sub></small> in DEGDME electrolyte. (a) The discharge/charge curves of the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C half cell (0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>), the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> half cell (0.5C) and the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell (0.5C). (b) The rate performance of the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell. (c) The cycling performance of the Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C full cell at 1C.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
    
    
      <h2 id="sect746"><span class="a_heading">Conclusions</span></h2>
      <span>In summary, the ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres with a tiny size of 3050 nm have been successfully synthesized <span class="italic">via</span> a simple hydrothermal route followed by a glucose carbonization treatment. When evaluated as an anode material for SIBs, the as-prepared ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/C nanospheres coupled with the EBE system exhibit significantly enhanced electrochemical performance, yielding a high specific capacity (241 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and outstanding cycling stability (209 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 3000 cycles with a low attenuation rate of 0.0031% per cycle). More impressively, an exceptional rate capability of 185 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> is also obtained at 20 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, demonstrating the best high-rate performance to date. The ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/CNa<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> full cell is designed and exhibits outstanding cycling performance (300 cycles at 1C). Such superior electrochemical behaviours originate from the intrinsic properties of ReS<small><sub>2</sub></small> nanospheres, the contribution of the surface carbon coating, and the favourable interaction of EBEs. Our findings provide new insights into the development of advanced LTMD electrodes for high-performance SIBs with EBEs.</span>
